I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
[Bug]: Continuous aggregates with time_bucket hourly and timezone fail to update
### What type of bug is this?

Incorrect result, Unexpected error

### What subsystems and features are affected?

Continuous aggregate

### What happened?

I have a number of Continuous aggregates that uses hourly buckets
```
 time_bucket(interval '1 hour', hypertable_name.time, 'Asia/Dubai')  AS bucket
 ```
 
 I noticed that i stopped seeing the new results after recreating the hypertable. After hours of debugging i pinned down that the hourly buckets dont refresh when used with timezone
 
 
![image](https://github.com/timescale/timescaledb/assets/42375159/6914e802-3fb7-4eb6-ad95-fcd1e0fcfaee)


### TimescaleDB version affected

2.14.2 and 2.15.0

### PostgreSQL version used

15.6

### What operating system did you use?

Arch Linux and Ubuntu Linux

### What installation method did you use?

Deb/Apt

### What platform did you run on?

On prem/Self-hosted

### Relevant log output and stack trace


### How can we reproduce the bug?

```bash
CREATE TABLE metrics (
    sensor_id INTEGER NOT NULL,
    value DOUBLE PRECISION NOT NULL,
    timestamp TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL
);
SELECT create_hypertable('metrics', 'timestamp');


-- insert data into the hyper table
INSERT INTO metrics
SELECT
    s.sensor_id,
    random()*50 + 10,
    timestamp
FROM
    generate_series(DATE (now() - interval '6 month'), (now() - interval '5 day'), INTERVAL '1 hours') AS timestamp
        CROSS JOIN (SELECT generate_series(1, 200) as sensor_id) as s;


-- hourly continuous aggregate with timezone
CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW datalake_hourly
WITH (timescaledb.continuous, timescaledb.materialized_only = true) AS
            SELECT
                time_bucket(INTERVAL '1 hour', metrics.timestamp, 'Asia/Dubai') AS bucket,
                sensor_id,
                count(*) as count_items
            FROM metrics
            GROUP BY bucket, sensor_id;
           


SELECT add_continuous_aggregate_policy(
        'datalake_hourly',
        start_offset => INTERVAL '3 months',
        end_offset => Null,
        schedule_interval => INTERVAL '15 seconds'
);        


-- insert few more rows
INSERT INTO metrics
SELECT
    s.sensor_id,
    random()*50 + 10,
    timestamp
FROM
    generate_series((now() - interval '5 day'), now(), INTERVAL '1 hour') AS timestamp
        CROSS JOIN (SELECT generate_series(1, 200) as sensor_id) as s;
        
-- wait and check the continuous aggregate
SELECT 
		timescaledb_information.jobs.job_id,
		timescaledb_information.jobs.application_name,
		timescaledb_information.jobs.initial_start,
		timescaledb_information.jobs.next_start,
		timescaledb_information.jobs.config,
		timescaledb_information.jobs.schedule_interval,
		timescaledb_information.jobs.max_runtime ,
		timescaledb_information.jobs.max_retries  ,   
		timescaledb_information.jobs.retry_period ,  
		timescaledb_information.jobs.scheduled ,
		timescaledb_information.jobs.fixed_schedule , 
		timescaledb_information.jobs.hypertable_name , 
		timescaledb_information.continuous_aggregates.view_name ,
		last_run_started_at ,
       job_status,
       last_run_status,
       last_successful_finish ,
       total_runs,
       total_failures ,
       total_successes 
FROM timescaledb_information.jobs
left join timescaledb_information.job_stats on timescaledb_information.jobs.job_id  =  timescaledb_information.job_stats.job_id 
left join timescaledb_information.continuous_aggregates on timescaledb_information.continuous_aggregates.materialization_hypertable_name  =  timescaledb_information.jobs.hypertable_name
order by job_id;
```

  1676	                 * 1. Monthly buckets
  1677	                 * 2. Buckets with timezones
  1678	                 * 3. Cases 1 and 2 at the same time
  1679	                 *
  1680	                 * For months we simply take 30 days like on interval_to_int64 and
  1681	                 * multiply this number by the number of months in the bucket. This
  1682	                 * reduces the task to days/hours/minutes scenario.
  1683	                 *
  1684	                 * Days/hours/minutes case is handled the same way as for fixed-sized
  1685	                 * buckets. The refresh window at least two buckets in size is adequate
  1686	                 * for such corner cases as DST.
  1687	                 */
  1688	
  1689	                /* bucket_function should always be specified for variable-sized buckets */
  1690	                Assert(bucket_function != NULL);
  1691	                /* ... and bucket_function->bucket_time_width too */
  1692	                Assert(bucket_function->bucket_time_width != NULL);
  1693	
  1694	                /* Make a temporary copy of bucket_width */
  1695	                Interval interval = *bucket_function->bucket_time_width;
  1696	                interval.day += 30 * interval.month;
  1697	                interval.month = 0;
  1698	                bucket_width = ts_interval_value_to_internal(IntervalPGetDatum(&interval), INTERVALOID);
  1699	        }
  1700	        else
  1701	        {
  1702	                bucket_width = ts_continuous_agg_fixed_bucket_width(bucket_function);
  1703	        }
  1704	
  1705	        return bucket_width;
  1706	}
  1707

#define JAN_3_2000 (2 * USECS_PER_DAY)

/*
 * The default origin is Monday 2000-01-03. We don't use PG epoch since it starts on a saturday.
 * This makes time-buckets by a week more intuitive and aligns it with date_trunc. Since month
 * bucketing ignores the day component this makes origin for month buckets 2000-01-01.
 */
#define DEFAULT_ORIGIN (JAN_3_2000)
#define TIME_BUCKET_TS(period, timestamp, result, shift)                                           \
	do                                                                                             \
	{                                                                                              \
		if ((period) <= 0)                                                                         \
			ereport(ERROR,                                                                         \
					(errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_PARAMETER_VALUE),                                     \
					 errmsg("period must be greater than 0")));                                    \
		/* shift = shift % period, but use TMODULO */                                              \
		TMODULO(shift, result, period);                                                            \
                                                                                                   \
		if (((shift) > 0 && (timestamp) < DT_NOBEGIN + (shift)) ||                                 \
			((shift) < 0 && (timestamp) > DT_NOEND + (shift)))                                     \
			ereport(ERROR,                                                                         \
					(errcode(ERRCODE_NUMERIC_VALUE_OUT_OF_RANGE),                                  \
					 errmsg("timestamp out of range")));                                           \
		(timestamp) -= (shift);                                                                    \
                                                                                                   \
		/* result = (timestamp / period) * period */                                               \
		TMODULO(timestamp, result, period);                                                        \
		if ((timestamp) < 0)                                                                       \
		{                                                                                          \
			/*                                                                                     \
			 * need to subtract another period if remainder < 0 this only happens                  \
			 * if timestamp is negative to begin with and there is a remainder                     \
			 * after division. Need to subtract another period since division                      \
			 * truncates toward 0 in C99.                                                          \
			 */                                                                                    \
			(result) = ((result) * (period)) - (period);                                           \
		}                                                                                          \
		else                                                                                       \
			(result) *= (period);                                                                  \
                                                                                                   \
		(result) += (shift);                                                                       \
	} while (0)

static void
validate_month_bucket(Interval *interval)
{
	/*
	 * Bucketing by a month and non-month cannot be mixed.
	 */
	Assert(interval->month);

	if (interval->day || interval->time)
	{
		ereport(ERROR,
				(errcode(ERRCODE_FEATURE_NOT_SUPPORTED),
				 errmsg("month intervals cannot have day or time component")));
	}
}

/*
 * To bucket by month we get the year and month of a date and convert
 * that to the nth month since origin. This allows us to treat month
 * bucketing similar to int bucketing. During this process we ignore
 * the day component and therefore only support bucketing by full months.
 */
static DateADT
bucket_month(int32 period, DateADT date, DateADT origin)
{
	int32 year, month, day;
	int32 result;

	j2date(date + POSTGRES_EPOCH_JDATE, &year, &month, &day);
	int32 timestamp = (year * 12) + month - 1;

	j2date(origin + POSTGRES_EPOCH_JDATE, &year, &month, &day);
	int32 offset = (year * 12) + month - 1;

	TIME_BUCKET(period, timestamp, offset, PG_INT32_MIN, PG_INT32_MAX, result);

	year = result / 12;
	month = result % 12;
	day = 1;

	return date2j(year, month + 1, day) - POSTGRES_EPOCH_JDATE;
}

/* Returns the period in the same representation as Postgres Timestamps.
 * Note that this is not our internal representation (microseconds).
 * Always returns an exact value.*/
static inline int64
get_interval_period_timestamp_units(Interval *interval)
{
	if (interval->month != 0)
	{
		ereport(ERROR,
				(errcode(ERRCODE_FEATURE_NOT_SUPPORTED),
				 errmsg("interval defined in terms of month, year, century etc. not supported")));

   413	 * Why two buckets? Note that the policy probably won't execute at at time
   414	 * that exactly aligns with a bucket boundary, so a window of one bucket
   415	 * might not cover a full bucket that we want to materialize:
   416	 *
   417	 * Refresh window:                   [-----)
   418	 * Materialized buckets:   |-----|-----|-----|
   419	 */
   420	static void
   421	validate_window_size(const ContinuousAgg *cagg, const CaggPolicyConfig *config)
   422	{
   423	        int64 start_offset;
   424	        int64 end_offset;
   425	        int64 bucket_width;
   426	
   427	        if (config->offset_start.isnull)
   428	                start_offset = ts_time_get_max(cagg->partition_type);
   429	        else
   430	                start_offset = interval_to_int64(config->offset_start.value, config->offset_start.type);
   431	
   432	        if (config->offset_end.isnull)
   433	                end_offset = ts_time_get_min(cagg->partition_type);
   434	        else
   435	                end_offset = interval_to_int64(config->offset_end.value, config->offset_end.type);
   436	
   437	        bucket_width = ts_continuous_agg_bucket_width(cagg->bucket_function);
   438	        Assert(bucket_width > 0);
   439	
   440	        if (ts_time_saturating_add(end_offset, bucket_width * 2, INT8OID) > start_offset)
   441	                ereport(ERROR,
   442	                                (errcode(ERRCODE_INVALID_PARAMETER_VALUE),
   443	                                 errmsg("policy refresh window too small"),
   444	                                 errdetail("The start and end offsets must cover at least"
   445	                                                   " two buckets in the valid time range of type \"%s\".",
   446	                                                   format_type_be(cagg->partition_type))));
   447	}
   448	
   449	static void
   450	parse_offset_arg(const ContinuousAgg *cagg, Oid offset_type, NullableDatum arg,
   451	                                 ContinuousAggPolicyOffset *offset)
   452	{
   453	        offset->isnull = arg.isnull;
   454	
   455	        if (!offset->isnull)
   456	        {
   457	                offset->value =
   458	                        convert_interval_arg(cagg->partition_type, arg.value, &offset_type, offset->name);
   459	                offset->type = offset_type;
   460	        }
   461	}

   337	 * Fill the fields of a integer based bucketing function

   341	                                                                                Datum *values)

   367	/*
   368	 * Fill the fields of a time based bucketing function
   369	 */
   370	static void
   371	cagg_fill_bucket_function_time_based(ContinuousAggBucketFunction *bf, bool *isnull, Datum *values)
   372	{
   373	        /*
   374	         * bucket_width
   375	         *
   376	         * The value is stored as TEXT since we have to store the interval value of time
   377	         * buckets and also the number value of integer based buckets.
   378	         */
   379	        Assert(!isnull[AttrNumberGetAttrOffset(Anum_continuous_aggs_bucket_function_bucket_width)]);
   380	        const char *bucket_width_str = TextDatumGetCString(
   381	                values[AttrNumberGetAttrOffset(Anum_continuous_aggs_bucket_function_bucket_width)]);
   382	        Assert(strlen(bucket_width_str) > 0);
   383	        bf->bucket_time_width = DatumGetIntervalP(
   384	                DirectFunctionCall3(interval_in, CStringGetDatum(bucket_width_str), InvalidOid, -1));
   385	
   386	        /* Bucket origin */
   387	        if (!isnull[AttrNumberGetAttrOffset(Anum_continuous_aggs_bucket_function_bucket_origin)])
   388	        {
   389	                const char *origin_str = TextDatumGetCString(
   390	                        values[AttrNumberGetAttrOffset(Anum_continuous_aggs_bucket_function_bucket_origin)]);

   392	                                                                                                                                           CStringGetDatum(origin_str),
   393	                                                                                                                                           ObjectIdGetDatum(InvalidOid),
   394	                                                                                                                                           Int32GetDatum(-1)));
   395	        }
   396	        else
   397	        {
   398	                TIMESTAMP_NOBEGIN(bf->bucket_time_origin);
   399	        }
   400	
   401	        /* Bucket offset */
   402	        if (!isnull[AttrNumberGetAttrOffset(Anum_continuous_aggs_bucket_function_bucket_offset)])
   403	        {
   404	                const char *offset_str = TextDatumGetCString(
   405	                        values[AttrNumberGetAttrOffset(Anum_continuous_aggs_bucket_function_bucket_offset)]);
   406	                bf->bucket_time_offset = DatumGetIntervalP(
   407	                        DirectFunctionCall3(interval_in, CStringGetDatum(offset_str), InvalidOid, -1));
   408	        }

   411	        if (!isnull[AttrNumberGetAttrOffset(Anum_continuous_aggs_bucket_function_bucket_timezone)])
   412	        {
   413	                bf->bucket_time_timezone = TextDatumGetCString(
   414	                        values[AttrNumberGetAttrOffset(Anum_continuous_aggs_bucket_function_bucket_timezone)]);
   415	        }

    57	
    58	static int64
    59	get_time_from_interval(const Dimension *dim, Datum interval, Oid type)
    60	{
    61	        Oid partitioning_type = ts_dimension_get_partition_type(dim);
    62	
    63	        if (IS_INTEGER_TYPE(type))
    64	        {
    65	                Oid now_func = ts_get_integer_now_func(dim, true);
    66	                int64 value = ts_interval_value_to_internal(interval, type);
    67	
    68	                Assert(now_func);
    69	
    70	                return ts_subtract_integer_from_now_saturating(now_func, value, partitioning_type);
    71	        }
    72	        else if (type == INTERVALOID)
    73	        {
    74	                Datum res = subtract_interval_from_now(DatumGetIntervalP(interval), partitioning_type);
    75	                return ts_time_value_to_internal(res, partitioning_type);
    76	        }
    77	        else
    78	                elog(ERROR, "unsupported offset type for continuous aggregate policy");
    79	
    80	        pg_unreachable();
    81	
    82	        return 0;
    83	}
    84	
    85	static int64
    86	get_time_from_config(const Dimension *dim, const Jsonb *config, const char *json_label,
    87	                                         bool *isnull)
    88	{
    89	        Oid partitioning_type = ts_dimension_get_partition_type(dim);
    90	        *isnull = false;
    91	
    92	        if (IS_INTEGER_TYPE(partitioning_type))
    93	        {
    94	                bool found;
    95	                int64 interval_val = ts_jsonb_get_int64_field(config, json_label, &found);
    96	
    97	                if (!found)
    98	                {
    99	                        *isnull = true;
   100	                        return 0;
   101	                }
   102	                return get_time_from_interval(dim, Int64GetDatum(interval_val), INT8OID);
   103	        }
   104	        else
   105	        {
   106	                Interval *interval_val = ts_jsonb_get_interval_field(config, json_label);
   107	
   108	                if (!interval_val)
   109	                {
   110	                        *isnull = true;
   111	                        return 0;
   112	                }
   113	
   114	                return get_time_from_interval(dim, IntervalPGetDatum(interval_val), INTERVALOID);
   115	        }
   116	}

   543	/*
   544	 * Execute refreshes based on the processed invalidations.
   545	 *
   546	 * The given refresh window covers a set of buckets, some of which are
   547	 * out-of-date (invalid) and some which are up-to-date (valid). Invalid
   548	 * buckets that are adjacent form larger ranges, as shown below.
   549	 *
   550	 * Refresh window:  [-----------------------------------------)
   551	 * Invalid ranges:           [-----] [-]   [--] [-] [---]
   552	 * Merged range:             [---------------------------)
   553	 *
   554	 * The maximum number of individual (non-mergeable) ranges are
   555	 * #buckets_in_window/2 (i.e., every other bucket is invalid).
   556	 *
   557	 * Since it might not be efficient to materialize a lot buckets separately
   558	 * when there are many invalid (non-adjecent) buckets/ranges, we put a limit
   559	 * on the number of individual materializations we do. This limit is
   560	 * determined by the MATERIALIZATIONS_PER_REFRESH_WINDOW setting.

   320	 *
   321	 * This function is called for an invalidation window before refreshing it and after the
   322	 * invalidation window was adjusted to be fully inside a refresh window. In the case of a
   323	 * continuous aggregate policy or manual refresh, the refresh window is the inscribed bucketed
   324	 * window.
   325	 *
   326	 * The circumscribed behaviour is also used for a refresh on drop, when the refresh is called during
   327	 * dropping chunks manually or as part of retention policy.
   328	 */
   329	InternalTimeRange
   330	compute_circumscribed_bucketed_refresh_window(const ContinuousAgg *cagg,
   331	                                                                                          const InternalTimeRange *const refresh_window,
   332	                                                                                          const ContinuousAggBucketFunction *bucket_function)
   333	{
   334	        Assert(cagg != NULL);
   335	        Assert(cagg->bucket_function != NULL);
   336	
   337	        if (bucket_function->bucket_fixed_interval == false)
   338	        {
   339	                InternalTimeRange result = *refresh_window;
   340	                ts_compute_circumscribed_bucketed_refresh_window_variable(&result.start,
   341	                                                                                                                                  &result.end,
   342	                                                                                                                                  bucket_function);
   343	                return result;
   344	        }
   345	
   346	        /* Interval is fixed */
   347	        int64 bucket_width = ts_continuous_agg_fixed_bucket_width(bucket_function);
   348	        Assert(bucket_width > 0);
   349	
   350	        InternalTimeRange result = *refresh_window;
   351	        InternalTimeRange largest_bucketed_window =
   352	                get_largest_bucketed_window(refresh_window->type, bucket_width);
   353	
   354	        /* Get offset and origin for bucket function */
   355	        NullableDatum offset = INIT_NULL_DATUM;
   356	        NullableDatum origin = INIT_NULL_DATUM;
   357	        fill_bucket_offset_origin(cagg, refresh_window, &offset, &origin);
   358	
   359	        /* Defined offset and origin in one function is not supported */
   360	        Assert(offset.isnull == true || origin.isnull == true);
   361	
   362	        if (refresh_window->start <= largest_bucketed_window.start)
   363	        {
   364	                result.start = largest_bucketed_window.start;
   365	        }
   366	        else
   367	        {
   368	                /* For alignment with a bucket, which includes the start of the refresh window, we just
   369	                 * need to get start of the bucket. */
   370	                result.start = ts_time_bucket_by_type_extended(bucket_width,
   371	                                                                                                           refresh_window->start,
   372	                                                                                                           refresh_window->type,
   373	                                                                                                           offset,
   374	                                                                                                           origin);
   375	        }
   376	
   377	        if (refresh_window->end >= largest_bucketed_window.end)
   378	        {
   379	                result.end = largest_bucketed_window.end;
   380	        }
   381	        else
   382	        {
   383	                int64 exclusive_end;
   384	                int64 bucketed_end;
   385	
   386	                Assert(refresh_window->end > result.start);
   387	
   388	                /* The end of the window is non-inclusive so subtract one before
   389	                 * bucketing in case we're already at the end of the bucket (we don't
   390	                 * want to add an extra bucket).  */
   391	                exclusive_end = ts_time_saturating_sub(refresh_window->end, 1, refresh_window->type);
   392	                bucketed_end = ts_time_bucket_by_type_extended(bucket_width,
   393	                                                                                                           exclusive_end,
   394	                                                                                                           refresh_window->type,
   395	                                                                                                           offset,
   396	                                                                                                           origin);
   397	
   398	                /* We get the time value for the start of the bucket, so need to add
   399	                 * bucket_width to get the end of it. */
   400	                result.end = ts_time_saturating_add(bucketed_end, bucket_width, refresh_window->type);
   401	        }
   402	        return result;
   403	}
   404

   406	 * Initialize the refresh state for a continuous aggregate.
   407	 *
   408	 * The state holds information for executing a refresh of a continuous aggregate.
   409	 */
   410	static void

   118	int64
   119	policy_refresh_cagg_get_refresh_start(const ContinuousAgg *cagg, const Dimension *dim,
   120	                                                                          const Jsonb *config, bool *start_isnull)
   121	{
   122	        int64 res = get_time_from_config(dim, config, POL_REFRESH_CONF_KEY_START_OFFSET, start_isnull);
   123	
   124	        /* interpret NULL as min value for that type */
   125	        if (*start_isnull)
   126	        {
   127	                Assert(cagg->partition_type == ts_dimension_get_partition_type(dim));
   128	                return cagg_get_time_min(cagg);
   129	        }
   130	
   131	        return res;
   132	}

   138

   205	                                                                                                                   materialization_id);
   206	        if (jobs == NIL)
   207	                return false;
   208	
   209	        return true;
   210	}

    71	         * that the Oid is mapped to a string when a backup is taken and the string is converted back to
    72	         * the Oid when the backup is restored. This way, we can use an Oid in the catalog table even

   356	/*
   357	 * Get the max for a time type in internal time.
   358	 */
   359	int64
   360	ts_time_get_max(Oid timetype)
   361	{
   362	        switch (timetype)
   363	        {
   364	                case DATEOID:
   365	                        return TS_DATE_INTERNAL_END - 1;
   366	                case TIMESTAMPOID:
   367	                        return TS_TIMESTAMP_INTERNAL_END - 1;
   368	                case TIMESTAMPTZOID:
   369	                        return TS_TIMESTAMP_INTERNAL_END - 1;
   370	                case INT2OID:
   371	                        return PG_INT16_MAX;
   372	                case INT4OID:
   373	                        return PG_INT32_MAX;
   374	                case INT8OID:
   375	                        return PG_INT64_MAX;
   376	                case UUIDOID:
   377	                        return TS_TIME_UUID_MAX;
   378	                default:
   379	                        break;
   380	        }
   381	
   382	        return ts_time_get_max(coerce_to_time_type(timetype));
   383	}
   384	
   385	/*
   386	 * Get the end value time for a time type in internal time.
   387	 *
   388	 * The end is not a valid time value (it is exclusive).
   389	 */
   390	int64
   391	ts_time_get_end(Oid timetype)
   392	{
   393	        switch (timetype)
   394	        {
   395	                case DATEOID:
   396	                        return TS_DATE_INTERNAL_END;
   397	                case TIMESTAMPOID:
   398	                        return TS_TIMESTAMP_INTERNAL_END;
   399	                case TIMESTAMPTZOID:
   400	                        return TS_TIMESTAMP_INTERNAL_END;
   401	                case INT2OID:
   402	                case INT4OID:
   403	                case INT8OID:
   404	                case UUIDOID:
   405	                        elog(ERROR, "END is not defined for \"%s\"", format_type_be(timetype));
   406	                        break;
   407	                default:
   408	                        break;
   409	        }
   410	
   411	        return ts_time_get_end(coerce_to_time_type(timetype));
   412	}
   413	
   414	/*
   415	 * Return the end (exclusive) or fall back to max.
   416	 *
   417	 * Integer time types have no definition for END, so we fall back to max.
   418	 */
   419	int64
   420	ts_time_get_end_or_max(Oid timetype)
   421	{
   422	        if (IS_TIMESTAMP_TYPE(timetype))
   423	                return ts_time_get_end(timetype);
   424	
   425	        return ts_time_get_max(timetype);
   426	}
   427	
   428	int64
   429	ts_time_get_nobegin(Oid timetype)
   430	{

   121	
   122	        PG_RETURN_INT64(watermark);
   123	}
   124	
   125	static int64
   126	cagg_compute_watermark(ContinuousAgg *cagg, int64 watermark, bool isnull)
   127	{
   128	        if (isnull)
   129	        {
   130	                watermark = ts_time_get_min(cagg->partition_type);
   131	        }
   132	        else
   133	        {
   134	                /*
   135	                 * The materialized hypertable is already bucketed, which means the
   136	                 * max is the start of the last bucket. Add one bucket to move to the
   137	                 * point where the materialized data ends.
   138	                 */
   139	                if (cagg->bucket_function->bucket_fixed_interval == false)
   140	                {
   141	                        /*
   142	                         * Since `value` is already bucketed, `bucketed = true` flag can
   143	                         * be added to ts_compute_beginning_of_the_next_bucket_variable() as
   144	                         * an optimization, if necessary.
   145	                         */
   146	                        watermark =
   147	                                ts_compute_beginning_of_the_next_bucket_variable(watermark, cagg->bucket_function);
   148	                }
   149	                else
   150	                {
   151	                        watermark =
   152	                                ts_time_saturating_add(watermark,
   153	                                                                           ts_continuous_agg_fixed_bucket_width(cagg->bucket_function),
   154	                                                                           cagg->partition_type);
   155	                }
   156	        }
   157	
   158	        return watermark;
   159	}

    65	 * Convert a Postgres TIMESTAMP to BIGINT microseconds relative the UNIX epoch.
    66	 */
    67	Datum
    68	ts_pg_timestamp_to_unix_microseconds(PG_FUNCTION_ARGS)
    69	{
    70	        TimestampTz timestamp = PG_GETARG_TIMESTAMPTZ(0);
    71	
    72	        if (TIMESTAMP_IS_NOBEGIN(timestamp))
    73	                PG_RETURN_INT64(TS_TIME_NOBEGIN);
    74	
    75	        if (TIMESTAMP_IS_NOEND(timestamp))
    76	                PG_RETURN_INT64(TS_TIME_NOEND);
    77	
    78	        if (timestamp < TS_TIMESTAMP_MIN)
    79	                ereport(ERROR,
    80	                                (errcode(ERRCODE_DATETIME_VALUE_OUT_OF_RANGE), errmsg("timestamp out of range")));

   124	                                 errdetail("A continuous aggregate references a hypertable that does not exist.")));

   126	        return ht;
   127	}
   128	
   129	/*
   130	 * Compute the largest possible bucketed window given the time type and
   131	 * internal restrictions.
   132	 *
   133	 * The largest bucketed window is governed by restrictions set by the type and
   134	 * internal, TimescaleDB-specific legacy details (see get_max_window above for
   135	 * further explanation).
   136	 */
   137	static InternalTimeRange
   138	get_largest_bucketed_window(Oid timetype, int64 bucket_width)
   139	{
   140	        InternalTimeRange maxwindow = {
   141	                .type = timetype,
   142	                .start = ts_time_get_min(timetype),
   143	                .end = ts_time_get_end_or_max(timetype),
   144	        };
   145	        InternalTimeRange maxbuckets = {
   146	                .type = timetype,
   147	        };
   148	
   149	        /* For the MIN value, the corresponding bucket either falls on the exact
   150	         * MIN or it will be below it. Therefore, we add (bucket_width - 1) to
   151	         * move to the next bucket to be within the allowed range. */
   152	        maxwindow.start = ts_time_saturating_add(maxwindow.start, bucket_width - 1, timetype);
   153	        maxbuckets.start = ts_time_bucket_by_type(bucket_width, maxwindow.start, timetype);
   154	        maxbuckets.end = ts_time_get_end_or_max(timetype);
   155	
   156	        return maxbuckets;
   157	}
   158	
   159	/*
   160	 * Adjust the refresh window to align with inscribed buckets, so it includes buckets, which are
   161	 * fully covered by the refresh window.
   162	 *
   163	 * Bucketing refresh window is necessary for a continuous aggregate refresh, which can refresh only
   164	 * entire buckets. The result of the function is a bucketed window, where its start is at the start
   165	 * of the first bucket, which is  fully inside the refresh window, and its end is at the end of the
   166	 * last fully covered bucket.
   167	 *
   168	 * Example1, the window needs to shrink:
   169	 *    [---------)      - given refresh window
   170	 * .|....|....|....|.  - buckets
   171	 *       [----)        - inscribed bucketed window
   172	 *
   173	 * Example2, the window is already aligned:
   174	 *       [----)        - given refresh window
   175	 * .|....|....|....|.  - buckets
   176	 *       [----)        - inscribed bucketed window
   177	 *
   178	 * This function is called for the continuous aggregate policy and manual refresh. In such case
   179	 * excluding buckets, which are not fully covered by the refresh window, avoids refreshing a bucket,
   180	 * where part of its data were dropped by a retention policy. See #2198 for details.

   664	static void
   665	emit_up_to_date_notice(const ContinuousAgg *cagg, const ContinuousAggRefreshContext context)
   666	{
   667	        switch (context.callctx)
   668	        {

   673	                                 NameStr(cagg->data.user_view_name));

   676	                case CAGG_REFRESH_POLICY_BATCHED:
   677	                        break;
   678	        }

   680	
   681	static bool
   682	process_cagg_invalidations_and_refresh(const ContinuousAgg *cagg,
   683	                                                                           const InternalTimeRange *refresh_window,
   684	                                                                           const ContinuousAggRefreshContext context, int32 chunk_id,
   685	                                                                           bool force)
   686	{
   687	        InvalidationStore *invalidations;
   688	        Oid hyper_relid = ts_hypertable_id_to_relid(cagg->data.mat_hypertable_id, false);
   689	
   690	        /* Lock the continuous aggregate's materialized hypertable to protect against
   691	         * concurrent invalidation log processing.
   692	         *
   693	         * It will produce rows in the `continuous_aggs_materialization_ranges` table
   694	         * to be materialized later either serially or in parallel for non-overlap
   695	         * refresh ranges.
   696	         *
   697	         * This is supposed to be a short transaction and in the future we can consider
   698	         * relaxing this lock.
   699	         */
   700	        LockRelationOid(hyper_relid, ExclusiveLock);
   701	        invalidations = invalidation_process_cagg_log(cagg,
   702	                                                                                                  refresh_window,
   703	                                                                                                  ts_guc_cagg_max_individual_materializations,
   704	                                                                                                  context,
   705	                                                                                                  force);
   706	        SPI_commit_and_chain();
   707	
   708	        DEBUG_WAITPOINT("after_process_cagg_invalidations_for_refresh_lock");
   709	
   710	        if (invalidations != NULL)
   711	        {
   712	                if (context.callctx == CAGG_REFRESH_CREATION)
   713	                {
   714	                        Assert(OidIsValid(cagg->relid));
   715	                        ereport(NOTICE,
   716	                                        (errmsg("refreshing continuous aggregate \"%s\"", get_rel_name(cagg->relid)),
   717	                                         errhint("Use WITH NO DATA if you do not want to refresh the continuous "
   718	                                                         "aggregate on creation.")));
   719	                }
   720	
   721	                continuous_agg_refresh_with_window(cagg, refresh_window, invalidations, chunk_id, context);
   722	                if (invalidations)
   723	                        invalidation_store_free(invalidations);
   724	                return true;
   725	        }
   726	
   727	        return false;
   728	}

   850	
   851	        /* Set the new invalidation threshold. Note that this only updates the
   852	         * threshold if the new value is greater than the old one. Otherwise, the
   853	         * existing threshold is returned. */
   854	        invalidation_threshold = invalidation_threshold_set_or_get(cagg, &refresh_window);
   855	
   856	        /* We must also cap the refresh window at the invalidation threshold. If
   857	         * we process invalidations after the threshold, the continuous aggregates
   858	         * won't be refreshed when the threshold is moved forward in the
   859	         * future. The invalidation threshold should already be aligned on bucket
   860	         * boundary. */
   861	        if (refresh_window.end > invalidation_threshold)
   862	                refresh_window.end = invalidation_threshold;
   863	
   864	        /* Capping the end might have made the window 0, or negative, so nothing to refresh in that
   865	         * case.
   866	         *
   867	         * For variable width buckets we use a refresh_window.start value that is lower than the
   868	         * -infinity value (ts_time_get_nobegin < ts_time_get_min). Therefore, the first check in the
   869	         * following if statement is not enough. If the invalidation_threshold returns the min_value for
   870	         * the data type, we end up with [nobegin, min_value] which is an invalid time interval.
   871	         * Therefore, we have also to check if the invalidation_threshold is defined. If not, no refresh
   872	         * is needed.  */
   873	        if ((refresh_window.start >= refresh_window.end) ||
   874	                (IS_TIMESTAMP_TYPE(refresh_window.type) &&
   875	                 invalidation_threshold == ts_time_get_min(refresh_window.type)))
   876	        {
   877	                emit_up_to_date_notice(cagg, context);
   878	
   879	                /* Restore search_path */
   880	                AtEOXact_GUC(false, save_nestlevel);
   881	
   882	                rc = SPI_finish();
   883	                if (rc != SPI_OK_FINISH)
   884	                        elog(ERROR, "SPI_finish failed: %s", SPI_result_code_string(rc));
   885	
   886	                return;
   887	        }
   888	
   889	        if (process_hypertable_invalidations)
   890	        {
   891	                /*
   892	                 * If we are using trigger-based invalidations, we can process the
   893	                 * invalidations for the associated hypertable only and later read the
   894	                 * invalidations for other hypertables, but when using WAL-based
   895	                 * invalidation we need to process all of the hypertables that are
   896	                 * currently using WAL.
   897	                 *
   898	                 * We want to prevent any changes to how invalidations are collected
   899	                 * in the meantime since changing the invalidation collection method
   900	                 * while this is running might cause problems and miss invalidations.
   901	                 *
   902	                 * Concurrency on the replication slot is controlled using some
   903	                 * special sauce in ReplicationSlotAcquire(), which is called inside
   904	                 * pg_logical_slot_get_changes_guts().
   905	                 *
   906	                 * This will currently generate an error rather than blocking on the
   907	                 * lock, so we need to add a separate lock to ensure a blocking
   908	                 * behaviour.
   909	                 */
   910	                if (has_invalidation_trigger(
   911	                                ts_hypertable_id_to_relid(cagg->data.raw_hypertable_id, false)))
   912	                        invalidation_process_hypertable_log(cagg->data.raw_hypertable_id, refresh_window.type);
   913	                else
   914	                        multi_invalidation_process_hypertable_log(get_all_wal_using_hypertables());
   915	        }
   916	
   917	        /* Commit and Start a new transaction */

  1143	                 * function and adding a 'verbose' parameter to is not useful for a

  1145	                 */

  1147	
  1148	                /*
  1149	                 * To determine inscribed/circumscribed refresh window for variable-sized
  1150	                 * buckets we should be able to calculate time_bucket(window.begin) and
  1151	                 * time_bucket(window.end). This, however, is not possible in general case.
  1152	                 * As an example, the minimum date is 4714-11-24 BC, which is before any
  1153	                 * reasonable default `origin` value. Thus for variable-sized buckets
  1154	                 * instead of minimum date we use -infinity since time_bucket(-infinity)
  1155	                 * is well-defined as -infinity.

   289	/*
   290	 * Compute a new invalidation threshold.
   291	 *
   292	 * The new invalidation threshold returned is the end of the given refresh
   293	 * window, unless it ends at "infinity" in which case the threshold is capped
   294	 * at the end of the last bucket materialized.
   295	 */
   296	int64
   297	invalidation_threshold_compute(const ContinuousAgg *cagg, const InternalTimeRange *refresh_window)
   298	{
   299	        bool max_refresh = false;
   300	        Hypertable *ht = ts_hypertable_get_by_id(cagg->data.raw_hypertable_id);
   301	
   302	        if (IS_TIMESTAMP_TYPE(refresh_window->type))
   303	                max_refresh = TS_TIME_IS_END(refresh_window->end, refresh_window->type) ||
   304	                                          TS_TIME_IS_NOEND(refresh_window->end, refresh_window->type);
   305	        else
   306	                max_refresh = TS_TIME_IS_MAX(refresh_window->end, refresh_window->type);
   307	
   308	        if (max_refresh)
   309	        {
   310	                bool isnull;
   311	                int64 maxval = ts_hypertable_get_open_dim_max_value(ht, 0, &isnull);
   312	
   313	                if (isnull)
   314	                {
   315	                        /* No data in hypertable */
   316	                        return cagg_get_time_min(cagg);
   317	                }
   318	                else
   319	                {
   320	                        if (cagg->bucket_function->bucket_fixed_interval == false)
   321	                        {
   322	                                return ts_compute_beginning_of_the_next_bucket_variable(maxval,
   323	                                                                                                                                                cagg->bucket_function);
   324	                        }
   325	
   326	                        int64 bucket_width = ts_continuous_agg_fixed_bucket_width(cagg->bucket_function);
   327	                        Assert(bucket_width > 0);
   328	                        int64 bucket_start = ts_time_bucket_by_type(bucket_width, maxval, refresh_window->type);
   329	                        /* Add one bucket to get to the end of the last bucket */
   330	                        return ts_time_saturating_add(bucket_start, bucket_width, refresh_window->type);
   331	                }
   332	        }
   333	
   334	        return refresh_window->end;
   335	}

cat > /tmp/tsrepro/full.sql <<'SQL'
\set ON_ERROR_STOP on
CREATE EXTENSION IF NOT EXISTS timescaledb;
CREATE TABLE metrics (
    sensor_id INTEGER NOT NULL,
    value DOUBLE PRECISION NOT NULL,
    timestamp TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL
);
SELECT create_hypertable('metrics', 'timestamp');
INSERT INTO metrics
SELECT s.sensor_id, random()*50 + 10, timestamp
FROM generate_series(DATE (now() - interval '6 month'), (now() - interval '5 day'), INTERVAL '1 hours') AS timestamp
CROSS JOIN (SELECT generate_series(1, 20) as sensor_id) as s;
CREATE MATERIALIZED VIEW datalake_hourly
WITH (timescaledb.continuous, timescaledb.materialized_only = true) AS
SELECT time_bucket(INTERVAL '1 hour', metrics.timestamp, 'Asia/Dubai') AS bucket,
       sensor_id, count(*) as count_items
FROM metrics GROUP BY bucket, sensor_id;
SELECT add_continuous_aggregate_policy('datalake_hourly', start_offset => INTERVAL '3 months', end_offset => Null, schedule_interval => INTERVAL '1 hour');
INSERT INTO metrics
SELECT s.sensor_id, random()*50 + 10, timestamp
FROM generate_series((now() - interval '5 day'), now(), INTERVAL '1 hour') AS timestamp
CROSS JOIN (SELECT generate_series(1, 20) as sensor_id) as s;
SELECT alter_job(job_id, scheduled => false) FROM timescaledb_information.jobs WHERE proc_name='policy_refresh_continuous_aggregate';
SELECT job_id, config FROM timescaledb_information.jobs WHERE proc_name='policy_refresh_continuous_aggregate';
CALL run_job((SELECT job_id FROM timescaledb_information.jobs WHERE proc_name='policy_refresh_continuous_aggregate'));
SQL
chown postgres:postgres /tmp/tsrepro/full.sql
psql -h localhost -p 55433 -U postgres -d postgres -v ON_ERROR_STOP=0 -f /tmp/tsrepro/full.sql > /tmp/tsrepro/full.out 2>&1; status=$?
echo STATUS=$status
cat /tmp/tsrepro/full.out | tail -100
cat /tmp/tsrepro/logfile | tail -80
runuser -u postgres -- /usr/lib/postgresql/17/bin/pg_ctl -D /tmp/tsrepro/data stop >/tmp/tsrepro/stop.log 2>&1 || true

   129	static inline int64
   130	cagg_get_time_min(const ContinuousAgg *cagg)
   131	{
   132	        if (cagg->bucket_function->bucket_fixed_interval == false)
   133	        {
   134	                /*
   135	                 * To determine inscribed/circumscribed refresh window for variable-sized
   136	                 * buckets we should be able to calculate time_bucket(window.begin) and
   137	                 * time_bucket(window.end). This, however, is not possible in general case.
   138	                 * As an example, the minimum date is 4714-11-24 BC, which is before any
   139	                 * reasonable default `origin` value. Thus for variable-sized buckets
   140	                 * instead of minimum date we use -infinity since time_bucket(-infinity)
   141	                 * is well-defined as -infinity.
   142	                 *
   143	                 * For more details see:
   144	                 * - ts_compute_inscribed_bucketed_refresh_window_variable()
   145	                 * - ts_compute_circumscribed_bucketed_refresh_window_variable()
   146	                 */
   147	                return ts_time_get_nobegin_or_min(cagg->partition_type);
   148	        }
   149	
   150	        /* For fixed-sized buckets return min (start of time) */
   151	        return ts_time_get_min(cagg->partition_type);
   152	}
   153	
   154	ContinuousAggBucketFunction *ts_cagg_get_bucket_function_info(Oid view_oid);
   155

   243	                        return Int16GetDatum(bucket_function->bucket_integer_offset);
   244	                case INT4OID:
   245	                        return Int32GetDatum(bucket_function->bucket_integer_offset);
   246	                case INT8OID:
   247	                        return Int64GetDatum(bucket_function->bucket_integer_offset);
   248	                default:
   249	                        elog(ERROR, "invalid integer time_bucket type \"%s\"", format_type_be(type));
   250	                        pg_unreachable();
   251	        }
   252	}
   253	
   254	/*
   255	 * Get a NullableDatum for offset and origin based on the CAgg information
   256	 */
   257	static void
   258	fill_bucket_offset_origin(const ContinuousAgg *cagg, const InternalTimeRange *const refresh_window,
   259	                                                  NullableDatum *offset, NullableDatum *origin)
   260	{
   261	        Assert(cagg != NULL);
   262	        Assert(offset != NULL);
   263	        Assert(origin != NULL);
   264	        Assert(offset->isnull);
   265	        Assert(origin->isnull);
   266	
   267	        if (cagg->bucket_function->bucket_time_based)
   268	        {
   269	                if (cagg->bucket_function->bucket_time_offset != NULL)
   270	                {
   271	                        offset->isnull = false;
   272	                        offset->value = IntervalPGetDatum(cagg->bucket_function->bucket_time_offset);
   273	                }
   274	
   275	                if (TIMESTAMP_NOT_FINITE(cagg->bucket_function->bucket_time_origin) == false)
   276	                {
   277	                        origin->isnull = false;
   278	                        if (refresh_window->type == DATEOID)
   279	                        {
   280	                                /* Date was converted into a timestamp in process_additional_timebucket_parameter(),
   281	                                 * build a Date again */
   282	                                origin->value = DirectFunctionCall1(timestamp_date,
   283	                                                                                                        TimestampGetDatum(
   284	                                                                                                                cagg->bucket_function->bucket_time_origin));
   285	                        }
   286	                        else
   287	                        {
   288	                                origin->value = TimestampGetDatum(cagg->bucket_function->bucket_time_origin);
   289	                        }
   290	                }
   291	        }
   292	        else
   293	        {
   294	                if (cagg->bucket_function->bucket_integer_offset != 0)
   295	                {
   296	                        offset->isnull = false;
   297	                        offset->value = int_bucket_offset_to_datum(refresh_window->type, cagg->bucket_function);
   298	                }
   299	        }
   300	}
   301	
   302	/*
   303	 * Adjust the refresh window to align with circumscribed buckets, so it includes buckets, which
   304	 * fully cover the refresh window.
   305	 *
   306	 * Bucketing refresh window is necessary for a continuous aggregate refresh, which can refresh only
   307	 * entire buckets. The result of the function is a bucketed window, where its start is at the start
   308	 * of a bucket, which contains the start of the refresh window, and its end is at the end of a
   309	 * bucket, which contains the end of the refresh window.
   310	 *
   311	 * Example1, the window needs to expand:
   312	 *    [---------)      - given refresh window
   313	 * .|....|....|....|.  - buckets
   314	 *  [--------------)   - circumscribed bucketed window
   315	 *

   330	
   331	typedef enum InvalidationResult
   332	{
   333	        INVAL_NOMATCH,
   334	        INVAL_DELETE,
   335	        INVAL_CUT,
   336	} InvalidationResult;
   337	
   338	#define IS_VALID_INVALIDATION(entry) ((entry)->hyper_id > 0)
   339	
   340	static bool
   341	save_invalidation_for_refresh(const ContinuousAggInvalidationState *state,
   342	                                                          const Invalidation *invalidation)
   343	{
   344	        if (!IS_VALID_INVALIDATION(invalidation))
   345	                return false;
   346	
   347	        int32 cagg_hyper_id = state->cagg->data.mat_hypertable_id;
   348	        TupleDesc tupdesc = RelationGetDescr(state->cagg_log_rel);
   349	        HeapTuple refresh_tup = create_invalidation_tup(tupdesc,
   350	                                                                                                        cagg_hyper_id,
   351	                                                                                                        invalidation->lowest_modified_value,
   352	                                                                                                        invalidation->greatest_modified_value);
   353	        tuplestore_puttuple(state->invalidations, refresh_tup);
   354	        heap_freetuple(refresh_tup);
   355	
   356	        InternalTimeRange refresh_window = {
   357	                .type = state->cagg->partition_type,
   358	                .start = invalidation->lowest_modified_value,
   359	                /* Invalidations are inclusive at the end, while refresh windows aren't, so add one to the
   360	                   end of the invalidated region */
   361	                .end = ts_time_saturating_add(invalidation->greatest_modified_value,
   362	                                                                          1,
   363	                                                                          state->cagg->partition_type),
   364	        };
   365	
   366	        InternalTimeRange bucketed_refresh_window =
   367	                compute_circumscribed_bucketed_refresh_window(state->cagg,
   368	                                                                                                          &refresh_window,
   369	                                                                                                          state->cagg->bucket_function);
   370	
   371	        insert_new_cagg_materialization_ranges(state, bucketed_refresh_window, cagg_hyper_id);
   372	
   373	        return true;
   374	}
   375	
   376	static void
   377	set_remainder_after_cut(Invalidation *remainder, int32 hyper_id, int64 lowest_modified_value,
   378	                                                int64 greatest_modified_value)
   379	{
   380	        MemSet(remainder, 0, sizeof(*remainder));
   381	        remainder->hyper_id = hyper_id;
   382	        remainder->lowest_modified_value = lowest_modified_value;
   383	        remainder->greatest_modified_value = greatest_modified_value;
   384	}
   385	
   386	/*
   387	 * Try to cut an invalidation against the refresh window.
   388	 *
   389	 * If an invalidation entry overlaps with the refresh window, it needs
   390	 * additional processing: it is either cut, deleted, or left unmodified.
   391	 *
   392	 * The part(s) of the invalidation that are outside the refresh window after
   393	 * the cut will remain in the log. The part of the invalidation that fits
   394	 * within the window is returned as the "remainder".
   395	 *
   396	 * Note that the refresh window is exclusive in the end while invalidations
   397	 * are inclusive.
   398	 */
   399	static InvalidationResult
   400	cut_invalidation_along_refresh_window(const ContinuousAggInvalidationState *state,
   401	                                                                          const Invalidation *invalidation,
   402	                                                                          const InternalTimeRange *refresh_window,
   403	                                                                          Invalidation *remainder)
   404	{
   405	        int32 cagg_hyper_id = state->cagg->data.mat_hypertable_id;
   406	        TupleDesc tupdesc = RelationGetDescr(state->cagg_log_rel);
   407	        InvalidationResult result = INVAL_NOMATCH;
   408	        HeapTuple lower = NULL;
   409	        HeapTuple upper = NULL;
   410	
   411	        Assert(remainder != NULL);
   412	
   413	        /* Entry is completely enclosed by the refresh window */
   414	        if (invalidation->lowest_modified_value >= refresh_window->start &&
   415	                invalidation->greatest_modified_value < refresh_window->end)
   416	        {
   417	                /*
   418	                 * Entry completely enclosed so can be deleted:
   419	                 *
   420	                 * [---------------)
   421	                 *     [+++++]
   422	                 */
   423	
   424	                result = INVAL_DELETE;
   425	                set_remainder_after_cut(remainder,
   426	                                                                cagg_hyper_id,
   427	                                                                invalidation->lowest_modified_value,
   428	                                                                invalidation->greatest_modified_value);
   429	        }
   430	        else
   431	        {
   432	                if (invalidation->lowest_modified_value < refresh_window->start &&
   433	                        invalidation->greatest_modified_value >= refresh_window->start)
   434	                {
   435	                        /*
   436	                         * Need to cut in right end:
   437	                         *
   438	                         *     [------)
   439	                         * [++++++]
   440	                         *
   441	                         * [++]
   442	                         */
   443	                        lower = create_invalidation_tup(tupdesc,
   444	                                                                                        cagg_hyper_id,
   445	                                                                                        invalidation->lowest_modified_value,
   446	                                                                                        refresh_window->start - 1);
   447	                        set_remainder_after_cut(remainder,
   448	                                                                        cagg_hyper_id,
   449	                                                                        refresh_window->start,
   450	                                                                        /* Refresh window not exclusive at end */
   451	                                                                        MIN(refresh_window->end - 1,
   452	                                                                                invalidation->greatest_modified_value));
   453	                        result = INVAL_CUT;
   454	                }
   455	
   456	                if (invalidation->lowest_modified_value < refresh_window->end &&
   457	                        invalidation->greatest_modified_value >= refresh_window->end)
   458	                {
   459	                        /*
   460	                         * If the invalidation is already cut on the left above, the reminder is set and
   461	                         * will be reset here. The assert prevents from losing information from the reminder.

str_replace_editor insert /testbed/src/ts_catalog/continuous_agg.c    --new_str '
/*
 * Convert a timestamp Datum to TimescaleDB'"'"'s internal representation, allowing
 * the exclusive upper timestamp bound (TS_TIMESTAMP_END). The regular
 * ts_time_value_to_internal() intentionally rejects TS_TIMESTAMP_END since it is
 * not a valid timestamp value for user data. However, continuous aggregate
 * refresh windows are half-open ranges and their end can legitimately be this
 * exclusive bound (for instance for open-ended policies). Variable-width bucket
 * alignment can preserve or produce exactly this bound, so keep it as the
 * internal END sentinel instead of raising "timestamp out of range".
 */
static int64
cagg_timestamp_to_internal_allow_end(Datum timestamp)
{
	if (DatumGetTimestamp(timestamp) == TS_TIMESTAMP_END)
		return ts_time_get_end(TIMESTAMPOID);

	return ts_time_value_to_internal(timestamp, TIMESTAMPOID);
}
' --insert_line 1495

/*
 * Convert a timestamp Datum to TimescaleDB's internal representation, allowing
 * the exclusive upper timestamp bound (TS_TIMESTAMP_END). The regular
 * ts_time_value_to_internal() intentionally rejects TS_TIMESTAMP_END since it is
 * not a valid timestamp value for user data. However, continuous aggregate
 * refresh windows are half-open ranges and their end can legitimately be this
 * exclusive bound (for instance for open-ended policies). Variable-width bucket
 * alignment can preserve or produce exactly this bound, so keep it as the
 * internal END sentinel instead of raising "timestamp out of range".
 */
static int64
cagg_timestamp_to_internal_allow_end(Datum timestamp)
{
        if (DatumGetTimestamp(timestamp) == TS_TIMESTAMP_END)
                return ts_time_get_end(TIMESTAMPOID);

        return ts_time_value_to_internal(timestamp, TIMESTAMPOID);
}


/*
 * Computes inscribed refresh_window for variable-sized buckets.
 *
 * The algorithm is simple:
 *
 * end = time_bucket(bucket_size, end)
 *
 * if(start != time_bucket(bucket_size, start))
 *     start = time_bucket(bucket_size, start) + interval bucket_size
 *
 */
void
ts_compute_inscribed_bucketed_refresh_window_variable(int64 *start, int64 *end,
                                                                                                          const ContinuousAggBucketFunction *bf)
{
        Datum start_old, end_old, start_aligned, end_aliged;

        /*
         * It's OK to use TIMESTAMPOID here. Variable-sized buckets can be used
         * only for dates, timestamps and timestamptz's. For all these types our
         * internal time representation is microseconds relative the UNIX epoch.
         * So the results will be correct regardless of the actual type used in
         * the CAGG. For more details see ts_internal_to_time_value() implementation.
         */
        start_old = ts_internal_to_time_value(*start, TIMESTAMPOID);
        end_old = ts_internal_to_time_value(*end, TIMESTAMPOID);

        start_aligned = generic_time_bucket(bf, start_old);
        end_aliged = generic_time_bucket(bf, end_old);

        if (DatumGetTimestamp(start_aligned) != DatumGetTimestamp(start_old))
        {
                start_aligned = generic_add_interval(bf, start_aligned);
        }

        *start = cagg_timestamp_to_internal_allow_end(start_aligned);
        *end = cagg_timestamp_to_internal_allow_end(end_aliged);
}

/*
 * Computes circumscribed refresh_window for variable-sized buckets.
 *
 * The algorithm is simple:
 *
 * start = time_bucket(bucket_size, start)
 *
 * if(end != time_bucket(bucket_size, end))
 *     end = time_bucket(bucket_size, end) + interval bucket_size
 */
void
ts_compute_circumscribed_bucketed_refresh_window_variable(int64 *start, int64 *end,
                                                                                                                  const ContinuousAggBucketFunction *bf)
{
        Datum start_old, end_old, start_new, end_new;

        /*
         * It's OK to use TIMESTAMPOID here.
         * See the comment in ts_compute_inscribed_bucketed_refresh_window_variable()
         */
        start_old = ts_internal_to_time_value(*start, TIMESTAMPOID);
        end_old = ts_internal_to_time_value(*end, TIMESTAMPOID);
        start_new = generic_time_bucket(bf, start_old);
        end_new = generic_time_bucket(bf, end_old);

        if (DatumGetTimestamp(end_new) != DatumGetTimestamp(end_old))
        {
                end_new = generic_add_interval(bf, end_new);
        }

        *start = cagg_timestamp_to_internal_allow_end(start_new);
        *end = cagg_timestamp_to_internal_allow_end(end_new);
}

/*
 * Calculates the beginning of the next bucket.
 *
 * The algorithm is just:
 *
 * val = time_bucket(bucket_size, val) + interval bucket_size
 */
int64
ts_compute_beginning_of_the_next_bucket_variable(int64 timeval,
                                                                                                 const ContinuousAggBucketFunction *bf)
{
        Datum val_new;
        Datum val_old;

        /*
         * It's OK to use TIMESTAMPOID here.
         * See the comment in ts_compute_inscribed_bucketed_refresh_window_variable()
         */
        val_old = ts_internal_to_time_value(timeval, TIMESTAMPOID);

        val_new = generic_time_bucket(bf, val_old);
        val_new = generic_add_interval(bf, val_new);
        return cagg_timestamp_to_internal_allow_end(val_new);
}

+/*
+ * Convert a timestamp Datum to TimescaleDB's internal representation, allowing
+ * the exclusive upper timestamp bound (TS_TIMESTAMP_END). The regular
+ * ts_time_value_to_internal() intentionally rejects TS_TIMESTAMP_END since it is
+ * not a valid timestamp value for user data. However, continuous aggregate
+ * refresh windows are half-open ranges and their end can legitimately be this
+ * exclusive bound (for instance for open-ended policies). Variable-width bucket
+ * alignment can preserve or produce exactly this bound, so keep it as the
+ * internal END sentinel instead of raising "timestamp out of range".
+ */
+static int64
+cagg_timestamp_to_internal_allow_end(Datum timestamp)
+{
+	if (DatumGetTimestamp(timestamp) == TS_TIMESTAMP_END)
+		return ts_time_get_end(TIMESTAMPOID);
+
+	return ts_time_value_to_internal(timestamp, TIMESTAMPOID);
+}

  * Computes inscribed refresh_window for variable-sized buckets.
